. (cc0130) Self-Care (9) E [Code the patient's usual performance at Discharge for each activity using the 6-point scale. If activity was not attempted at Discharge, code the reason, Coding: Safety and Quality of Performance ~ if helper assistance is required because patient's performance is unsafe or of poor quality, score according fo amount of assistance provided, Activities may be completed with or without assistive devices. 06. Independent ~ Patient completes the activity by him/herself with no assistance from a helper, 05. Setup or clean-up assistance - Helper sets up or cleans up; patient completes activity. Helper assists only prior to or following the activity, 04. Supervision or touching assistance ~ Helper provides verbal cues and/or touching/steadying and/or contact guard assistance as patient completes activity. Assistance may be provided throughout the activity or intermittently. 03, Partiallmoderate assistance ~ Helper does LESS THAN HALF the effort. Helper lifts, holds or supports trunk or limbs, but provides less than half the effort. 02. Substantial/maximal assistance ~ Helper does MORE THAN HALF the effort. Helper lifts or holds trunk or limbs and provides more than half the effort. 01. Dependent — Helper does ALL of the effort. Patient does none of the effort to complete the activity. Or, the assistance of 2 or more helpers is required for the patient to complete the activity. If activity was not attempted, code reason: 07. Patient refused 09. Not applicable - Not attempted and the patient did not perform this activity prior to the current illness, exacerbation or injury. 10. Not attempted due to environmental limitations (e.g,, lack of equipment, weather constraints) 88. Not attempted due to medical conditions or safety concerns 3. Diagnoses are listed in the order that best z reflects the seriousness of each condition and supports the disciplines and services provided. Rate the degree of symptom control for each condition in Sg Column 2, (CD-10-CM sequencing requirements must be followed if multiple coding is indicated for any diagnoses. 2 B Code each row according to the following directions for each column: ra Column 1: Enter the description of the diagnosis. Sequencing of diagnoses should reflect the seriousness of each condition and support the disciplines and ‘ services provided. Column 2: Enter the ICD-10-CM code for the condition described in Column 1 - no surgical or procedure codes allowed. Codes must be entered at the level of highest specificity and ICD-10-CM coding rules and sequencing requirements must be followed. Note that external cause codes (ICD-10-CM codes beginning with V, W, X, or Y) may not be reported in M1021 (Primary Diagnosis) but may be reported in M1023 (Secondary Diagnoses). Also note that when a Z-code is reported in Column 2, the code for the underlying condition can often be entered in Column 2, as long as itis an active on-going condition impacting home health care, Rate the degree of symptom control for the condition listed in Column 1, Do not assign a symptom control rating if the diagnosis code is a V, W, X, Y or Z-code, Choose one value that represents the degree of symptom control appropriate for each diagnosis using the following scale: 0- Asymptomatic, no treatment needed at this time 1- Symptoms well controlled with current therapy 2- Symptoms controlled with difficulty, affecting daily functioning; patient needs ongoing monitoring 3- Symptoms poorly controlled; patient needs frequent adjustment in treatment and dose monitoring 4- Symptoms poorly controlled; history of re-hospitalizations Note that the rating for symptom control in Column 2 should not be used to determine the sequencing of the diagnoses listed in Column 1, These are separate items and sequencing may not coincide, (mio21) Primary Diagnosis & (i023) Other Diagnoses Column 4 Po Column Diagnoses(Sequencing of diagnosis should reflect the seriousness of each condition |/CD-10-CM and symptom control rating for each condition.Note that the and support the disciplines and services provided) sequencing of these ratings may not match sequencing of the diagnoses Description ICD-10-CM / Symptom Control Rating (wio21} Primary Diagnosis V,.W, X,Y codes NOT allowed . a, (M62.81 ) a. Describe Today’s Interventions/Response to Treatment - (Verbal/Tactile Cues, Activity Focus, Volume/Duration/Complexity, RPE) Ambulated with pt outside, told pt to bring her SPC just in case she needed it; we walked the outer perimeter of the yard with no problem, walking up the ramp to front porch and pt's foot slid out of shoe (Slide shoe), pt was holding onto railing which eased her fall; pt landed on her right side, pt sat up right away; told her not to move, notice a skin tear on right forearm and 2 knots, lumps that came up: 1 on lateral side of forearm and the other lateral side of wrist. Explained to pt that I needed to call EMS; pt stated, "No, don't call them!" Contacted Dr. Maderic's office and spoke with nursing assistance (Amanda) and explained what had happened and that pt would not go to the ER and her. arm needed to be X-rayed; Amanda stated that Dr. Maderic had an opening at 1:00 PM. Pt's husband was not home at the time, contacted him and explained what had happened, stated that he was 10 minutes away. While waiting for husband cleaned area with bottled water, did not have any saline, wrapped right arm with a clean towel with 2 ice packs. Asked pt if she was having any pain; pt stated, "No.". Pt did not hit her head, her right knee had a little scrape on it as well. Assisted husband with getting pt in the car; asked pt how she felt, stated that she was a little dizzy.; Asked pt if she was dizzy when we were walking; pt stated, "No."

Pt not wearing proper foot wear (slide sandals); pt's husband said that is all she wears. Explained to pt that she needed to get shoes that have a back on them; pt verbalized understanding.
